<username>Anna Wang<//username>< text>
Beware of hidden fees when you rent from the leasing office. Regents La Jolla is the best community around UCSD, but there are two types of owners and renters need to consider the differences. The leasing office owns a lot of units in this complex. Please remember that on top of rent, renters need to pay for water, trash, sewer, etc if you deal with the leasing office. These fees vary each month, below is an example of the bill. You can see that the fees amount to $78. If you rent from individual owners, they only charge you rent (maybe plus water, but definitely no trash and sewer). So when compare the two prices, make sure that you'll pay more monthly if you rent from the leasing office. But I'm not saying that renting from the leasing office doesn't have advantage.  if you have problems with plumbing, appliances, etc, the leasing office will dispatch repair workers very soon (usually the same day) and if you rent from individual owner, you probably need to wait for a few days for the repair to be done. So I'm not saying that the extra bucks are not worth it, I'm just pointing out that they are there.</text>

< Text>
Really cool location.  Parking is a breeze.  Atmosphere is alive and loud at peak times.  Staff are helpful, knowledgable and accommodating.  Scallop appetizer is really special- very good.  I ordered mushroom pasta and it came out a bit dry but flavors were there.  We had a late dinner so maybe that had something to do with it.  The fish was good and served with potato and long stemmed arugula.  All in all a fun place to be.  I would get like 3 scallops and a salad after I enjoyed one of their amazing artisan cocktails.  After dining take a lap around the fountain in the courtyard.<//Text>

<userid>103779963086077677864<//userid>< user_name>
Amanda Pfluger</user_name>
< Time>
1539146945171< /Time>
<Rating>5<//Rating>< Text>
This is going to sound weird, but the funghi pasta made me cry. It was that good.

Yes, I am a crier, but there were so many other things that we're good about this place that the whole experience is definitely 5 stars.

I usually don't like seeing truffle oil or truffle stuff on a dish. I feel like it can overpower the whole thing, and some restaurants just dribble it at the end and it really doesn't go with other flavors of the dish. It's just a nice pricey add-on at the end. That was not the case with this dish. The truffle cheese melted on your tongue and mingled with every different mushroom they had (I counted 4 I think). I loved separating them to taste each unique flavor for some bites, and then shoving them all in at once cause they worked so well together! I am an umami fiend. It's kind of a problem actually.. But anyway this dish just drowned me in earthy umami flavor and I just wanted to sit and suffocate in it all.

My cocktail (can't remember which one, sorry) was a touch too sweet for me. My wine pairing was perfect, our antipasto misto was delicious, and my husband had the osso buco which was good but I just wanted to eat my freakin pasta.

My husband forced me to tell the waitress to let the chef know I was brought to tears. I think she thought I was exaggerating, but she said the chef appreciated it.

Wheelchair accessible, cute little brick building, nice open, dimly lit restaurant. Romantic <3< /Text>

< Review>
One of our top 3 fav places.  We are pescatarian and there's always a great selection for us. Soups,  salads,  and main dishes plus appetzers... Soups are amazing.. (want a cup?  Get a bowl and take some home!!) . Wonderful wine selection, particularly (but not only) on a warm day,  start your meal w one of their Lambrusco's if it's available.  Service is friendly w knowledgeable staff.  Great mixed drink options also. Easy parking,  quiet neighborhood.  Have never been there for lunch,  but outdoor seating is amazing... It's in a spot where eating outside at dinner is rare (fog rlls in)  but can imagine it's wonderful for lunch.< /Review>

I didn't have the best experience with this company. A few things:

1. My personal credit score took a 100 point hit. Apparently a "soft hit" is really not soft. I made it clear I wanted to build my business credit. Why is 2 of 6 cards in the business name and I can't use 1 because it had hidden fees I was not made aware of from the beginning.
2. I wasn't even approved for the amount I needed which was within the limits of the contract. So really can't purchase the things I needs to benefit my business.
3. Be mindful some the credit cards they will approve you for might not have a 0% interest on payments or balance transfer. So if you need to purchase now and pay later, probably not the company for you. Also some credit cards will have an annual membership fee as well your agent won't tell you until you are approved. I am guessing these are things they should know or ATLEAST make you aware of before you signed a $995 non refundable contract.
4. You will potentially spend alot of time on the phone with you financial advisor during the entire process when talking with banks. So literally this is NOT a HANDS OFF process. Make time for lots of three way calls. So you are literally paying for someone to give companies your application because you still have to do 90% of the leg work.
5.  I can only really utilize 4 of 6 of the credit cards I was approved for. The amount  of credit the 4 equate for is less than the minimum amount they promised I will qualify for.
6. Lastly, I made it very clear I need to have a substantial amount of cash available and not all  the funds tied up in credit cards, that didn't happen. I received credit cards only and they all have a 20% and higher to take cash from them. Not worth it.

BE CAREFUL with this company. They are not for everyone. Not the happiest customer, but don't worry Seek capital I paid my invoice because one of us needs to be honorable and keep our word.< /review>

<Text>As any start up knows, finding the capital in the beginning is absolutely tough. This was a good way to get capital fast and was better than the traditional routes for speed and access.  What you  have to know is that you aren't getting a loan or funding, you are paying someone to scrub the current credit cards out there and open accounts on your behalf.  I was ok paying someone to do this. Initially had some problems with the original account manager, but they did a good job fixing the situation and getting the funding I needed. The only two items to be careful with are funding amounts, and credit scores.

I originally asked for an signed an agreement for funding of $40K - $60K. Because they are going out and applying for credit at several places, it's possible to over fund. When I reached my needed amount, I thought I was done, but then got a call and invoice for more funding. It's ok to push back, not activate the card and say no thank you.

The other thing that will happen is your credit score will go down. Mine dropped by almost 150 points, which I was not ready for. This happened even though I had only used about $6000 in funding. Just something to watch out for and closing the accounts of the cards you don't need helps.

I would definitely use them again especially for a company that just starting or has less then 2 years.< /Text>< pictures>

<user_id>112912086245753378490</user_id><Name>Yossy<//Name><date>1555383740298<//date><rate>2< /rate>< review>
Seek Capital is a very well put together company, from the scripts their employees follow, to the legal paperwork they force you to sign. This set up make you believe you can trust them, but after you sign the first set of documents, new rules and regulations start coming along the process, and there is no going back, unless you pay the price.
We were seeking $50,000 to fund a brand new business, so we where offer a combination of personal and business credit cards to achieve our goal. According to them, It was "easy goal" after they check our credit report. We did NOT agreed to the personal credit cards, so we were told we could get about $30K on business credit cards. We agreed to the business credit cards only. Then they presented a proposal to us where "personal credit cards" was listed as part of the deal. They said they had to talk to the underwriting team to change the proposal... but guess what people: at this point they already knew our ENTIRE financial and personal life, and we had singed some documents.... either we kept moving or pay the price...
They did numerous inquiries on our credit report, and like everybody else has reviewed, the credit score was dramatically affected.
They applied for credit card companies I already have relationship with, easy on their end... but I had to do all the calling and the follow up with each one of them... My question is: Why the hell they made us sign a power of attorney for, then? At the end we got $20K in personal credit cards which if we decide to cash-out we have to use another financial company, which according to them is not affiliated to Seek Capital and you have to pay them too. By the way, the fees Seek Capital charges are insane. Last  but not least, the reason Seek Capital doesn't have less than 3-stars is because they make you initial a document that says you can't make negative reviews about the "company" on social media or any website... and by "company" it wasn't clear if it was Seek Capital, or not,... they might be violating First Amendment of the constitution.
People, from the bottom of my heart, seek financing with your banks... it might take longer to get approve, but at the end of the day you are going to save so much money and you'll have more room for growth.< /review>

<Name>Ron< /Name><Gmap_id>0x80c2b938eb517099:0xb959748e99f0c0d1< /Gmap_id>< text>
I had looked at a few different options for my new business as far as funding is concerned.  One was an SBA (too long to get going), one was a re-fi on my house and another was using my IRA with converting my business to a C-Corp.  My CPA told me that C-Corp's are a nightmare, so that one was out.  I didn't want to go through a re-fi either.

I looked into Seek and they had the best turnaround time that I had been quoted.  If you have a solid credit rating then you will have no issues.  In fact, some of the cards came before I had expected.  Everyone I worked with was great to do business with.  Very professional.

They will tell you that there is a 99 percent fail rate in securing an SBA loan (not true). There are many great SBA options out there for new start-ups. They just want to sell you on unsecured business credit in the form of credit cards, which is fine. Do not sign their initial agreement. I signed the agreement and then called them a few hours later to tell them to hold off before speaking with lenders. I wanted to look into SBA options first.
They are invoicing me for $500 as a cancellation fee and they did absolutely no work towards helping me or my business other than a ten minute qualification call.

I feel like a kid being beat up on the playground for his lunch money.  Any business with common sense or integrity, would not have a $1,000 dollar cancellation clause on an initial agreement after a ten minute qualification call. That should be a red flag right there for everyone. Seek will do well in the short term because they shake everyone down for money, ten years from now they will not be around though because they are building their business on sales tactics and cancellation threats instead of on what's best for their potential clients. Do what is best for your customer and the money will always follow. Seek, at least with me, was money first, what's best for me..... second.

Solution:

Check out Guidant Financial. They can help with 401k rollovers for new business start ups as well as help secure SBA loans for lower interest rates. They have been very accommodating. Plus, although they took my credit card information, they didn't charge me a dime until we had several conference calls, they began speaking to lenders, and they were confident they could help me.  (business integrity).

The plan administration through Guidant gets terrible reviews so maybe consider using another company for administrative purposes once your 401k plan is established for your new small business. Call Guidant and ask them about their 401k rollover program and the help they can provide with SBA loan lenders. It is expensive, but well worth it.  Feel free to contact me with any questions.<//Text>
